Hangzhou 106

Suicide of a Traveler at the West Lake Hotel: A young traveler came to the West Lake Hotel in Xinchang Market at 11:00 PM on the 3rd of this month and booked Room 112. He identified himself as Cheng Ziwen, a 21-year-old from Nanjing, and carried a suitcase. After entering the room and going to bed, he had not gotten up by noon the next day. The waiter called him but received no response. Upon entering the room, the waiter found the young man's face pale, and a broken bottle of sleeping pills was on the floor next to the bed. He quickly informed the front desk, who reported it to the Second District Police Station. The police station dispatched a health officer, Wu Jiaxing, who found the guest unable to speak. He hired a car to send him to the Hangzhou Hospital for treatment. However, the poisoning was too severe, and he died at 5:00 AM on the 5th. The traveler left behind five letters, a medical lecture, a small wallet containing five yuan and two jiao in silver coins, two military notes, a steel watch, a fountain pen, a medical badge, a pair of leather shoes, a copper basin hat, and a Western-style suit. After investigation, the guest's real name was Chen Huan, and he was studying at the Provincial Medical School. His brother, Chen Zhongken, is the director of the military medical department at the Nanjing Garrison Command. The cause of death is believed to be related to love. The contents of the letters to the principal and friends are unknown. At 2:00 PM, Prosecutor Jiang Lichun from the court led the coroner and others to examine the body and confirmed that he died from poisoning. The letters were kept in the court, and the deceased's cousin, Chen Gao, and younger brother, Chen Yunxi, prepared a coffin and arranged for the body to be temporarily placed in the Siming Guild Hall while they telegraphed his brother in Hangzhou.

Sister-in-law and Sister Fight over Love, Attempt Suicide by Jumping into River: In Linjiang Village, eight miles from Yaqian in Dongxiang, a man named Shi set up a small school in the Land Temple and hired Ge, a young and handsome man from Xinchang, as a teacher. Ge fell in love with Yin Xing, a Lin girl in the back house. Feng Gu, Yin Xing's sister-in-law, also became involved with Ge. The teacher was enjoying the happiness of a double love affair. On the 31st of last month, the sisters-in-law suddenly had a lovers' quarrel. Yin Xing, feeling ashamed, jumped into the river to end her life. Seeing the trouble she caused, the sister-in-law also jumped into the pond behind the temple. Neighbors heard the commotion and rushed to rescue them, but they were both barely alive.

Anqing 109

Huayang River Dredging Measures Involving Seven Counties in Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangxi Provinces: The Huayang River dredging project, which concerns the water conservancy of the three provinces of Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangxi and seven counties, has been stalled for a long time. Recently, the Anhui Provincial Government approved the consultation order from the Ministry of Internal Affairs and ordered the Civil Affairs and Construction Departments to draft appropriate measures to be submitted. The two departments have now drafted measures and jointly submitted them to the provincial government. The content is divided into three steps: First, according to Jiangxi's proposal, the three provinces will send personnel to jointly conduct an on-site survey to formulate a measurement plan and budget. Second, according to Anhui's proposal, the original plan for cost sharing in 1919 (Anhui Province shares 51%, Hubei Province shares 39%, and Jiangxi Province shares 10%) will be followed, and the three provincial governments will be responsible for the measurement expenses and organize a measurement team to conduct precise measurements and finalize the construction plan. Third, according to Hubei's proposal, the beneficiary owners and gentry of the three provinces and seven counties will jointly raise funds for construction, so that both the government and the people can be considered, and practical actions can be taken. The provincial government believes that the proposed measures are largely in line with the opinions of Hubei and Jiangxi provinces and are feasible. Yesterday, it informed the Hubei and Jiangxi provincial governments of the situation and requested that they verify and respond so that the river dredging project can be gradually realized.

The Ministry of Education will pay closer attention to schools at all levels to ensure that non-party factions can be assimilated.

Cancellation of "Billion" and "Trillion" in Mathematical Calculations 111

The Ministry of Education, based on a request from the Chung Hwa Book Company regarding the proposal to discontinue the use of "billion" and "trillion" beyond ten thousand in the decimal counting system, issued an order to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities. The order states that the Chung Hwa Book Company submitted a report stating that the method of dividing numbers above a thousand in the decimal counting systems of China and foreign countries has been different. China has two methods of division. One is to use "ten thousand" as "billion" and "million" (that is, ten "billion") as "trillion," with one section of seven digits per unit. The other is to use "ten thousand ten thousand" as "billion" and "ten thousand billion" as "trillion." The calculation is one, ten, one hundred, one thousand, ten thousand, ten ten thousand, one hundred ten thousand, one thousand ten thousand, "billion," ten "billion," one hundred "billion," one thousand "billion," "trillion," ten "trillion," one hundred "trillion," one thousand "trillion," with one section per four digits. The world's common section system uses three digits per section, so there is a slight change per thousand. Therefore, "ten thousand" is ten thousand, and one million is another name called "Million." Ten thousand ten thousand is called "Billion." In Chinese books, the numbers above ten thousand often use names such as "billion" and "trillion." The so-called "billion" refers to ten thousand or ten thousand ten thousand. The so-called "trillion" refers to one million or ten thousand billion, which is impossible to determine. Now, if a seven-digit section system is used, another name must be given above "trillion." The original word "ladder" has long been out of use and seems unfamiliar. If a four-digit section system is used, although it is neat and unified, it is not very consistent with the world's common three-digit section system. Now, the numbers in the official accounting and statistics system have uniformly adopted a three-digit section system, while the ordinary text and even the textbooks in schools still use names such as "billion" and "trillion." Numbers are used to seek accuracy and avoid ambiguity, but now the use of words like "billion" and "trillion" increases inaccuracy, which is contradictory to the application of numbers. The agency has realized this, and after editing the book, it plans to remove the ambiguous words of "billion" and "trillion." All numbers above ten thousand are cumulatively prefixed above the word "ten thousand," such as ten ten thousand, one hundred ten thousand, one thousand ten thousand, ten thousand ten thousand, and one hundred thousand ten thousand. Although it feels a bit cumbersome, the calculation of the number seems more accurate. But this is a matter of custom, and the agency does not dare to specialize. Whether there is a case should be submitted to the unit for deliberation. If it is considered feasible, should it be promulgated nationwide to show uniformity? Otherwise, please ask the unit to verify and indicate a method to follow. For the above reasons such as all decimal counting systems above ten thousand do not use "billion" and "trillion" digits that are cumulatively prefixed above the word "ten thousand," is it feasible? I respectfully ask your unit to review and approve the instructions to follow. In addition to the investigation of the request to not use the two words "billion" and "trillion" and to use the cumulative prefix above the word "ten thousand" for all decimal counting systems, it is not without merit that a counting term has not been determined before it should be temporarily approved. If the bureau has already adopted the two words "billion" and "trillion" in each textbook, it should uniformly follow the revision in the next edition. In addition to the order to comply to show uniformity, please inform, etc., and it is hereby ordered that the provincial offices follow the same command.

Tai Shuangqiu, Xie Xunchu, Bao Qibao, Zhang Zhongdao, Wang Maozu, Zhang Shiyi, Peng Baichuan, Zhang Yaoxiang, Yang Zhenxian, Wang Shulin, Xu Keshi, Xia Chengfeng, Hu Changcai, Ma Jingxuan, Li Qingsong, Zhu Dingjun, and other educators in Beijing and Shanghai, totaling over two hundred people, have proposed June 6th as Teacher's Day. Local News

Purpose of the Municipal Education Bureau's Unification of Teaching Materials 114

Order all bookstores to send reviewed books for reference.

Strictly order not to use textbooks that have not been reviewed by the Ministry of Education again.

Dear Editor, I recently read a news item in the education news column of your newspaper about the Education Bureau unifying textbooks. The Bureau previously found that most schools in the city use textbooks reviewed and approved by the Ministry of Education, but quite a few still use unreviewed textbooks. To ensure the unification of teaching materials in all schools in the city, the Bureau ordered all bookstores to submit two copies of textbooks that have been reviewed and approved by the Ministry of Education for display and reference. At the same time, it strictly ordered all schools not to use unreviewed textbooks again. This is the Bureau's intention to unify teaching materials. Fearing that the public is unaware of the truth, I ask that you make a correction. To the Shin Pao Newspaper Office.

The International Games Open Today 117

Children from Nine Countries Dedicate Themselves This Afternoon at 2 PM

The Chinese Team is Well-Rounded and Full of Hope

The Shanghai International Track and Field Games, which have caused a sensation, will open at 1:45 PM today at the China Track and Field Stadium on Route Pere Robert. This event brings together the best of Shanghai and the most renowned athletes from the East and West. 200 child heroes from nine countries will compete and contend, making this a fierce and exciting competition. The Chinese team is well-rounded and has the highest hopes of winning.

Venue Arrangement 118

Sumptuous and magnificent, the entrance to the venue is a cypress archway erected at the corner of Route Pere Robert and Route Say Po Sai, towering several meters high and draped in national flags, fluttering in the wind and smiling to welcome people. In the center of the venue, there is a pavilion-style command platform with the national flag flying on top, creating a magnificent atmosphere. On the side of the 100-meter starting point, there are seven rural-style reed sheds for the athletes from various countries to rest. The area is surrounded by colorful national flags, which are beautiful and pleasing to the eye. At the end of the 100-meter mark, there is a press stand for reporters to record news.

The arrangements are comprehensive. The association has always been presided over by Westerners. This session was taken back by the China National Sports Association to organize. After months of preparation, the equipment has been completed. The sporting equipment is based on the new rules of the World Games. The running track is divided into lanes with white powder. The black and white are quite clear.

Order is maintained by Boy Scouts from Guanghua, American and Chinese schools. Non-staff members and athletes are not allowed to enter the venue to facilitate the competition.

The military band of the British and American navies will be on hand to play music to help boost the spirit of the athletes. The results in the stadium will be announced using the large loudspeaker of the Municipal Government, and the results will be broadcasted by the Tianling Company using wireless radio to all cities. Viewing all the arrangements, it can be said that the utmost perfection has been achieved.

Free Talk

World Tidbits 131

— Sea Guest

A famous British female doctor declared that if women could fully rest for one hour each day with their legs raised above their heads, it would benefit their hearts, prevent varicose veins, and plump up their ankles to prevent them from becoming too slender.

In 1922, approximately 60,000 households in the United States had radios. Now, that number has skyrocketed to 10 million households, with at least 40 million listeners. The development of their radio industry is astounding.

About two hundred members of the British House of Lords permanently reside within the building, including the clerks, attendants, cooks, and firefighters who handle daily affairs.

There are numerous correspondence schools in the United States, and universities often have affiliated correspondence programs. The correspondence subjects are categorized extensively. Recently, a certain university added a correspondence course for aviation, which is the newest record.

Stratford-on-Avon, a town on the River Avon in England, is the hometown of the great playwright Shakespeare. Recently, an initiative to build a Shakespeare Memorial Theatre was launched. In the United States, 2,000 people enthusiastically donated money. The list of these 2,000 people is bound in a particularly large volume, weighing 200 catties, requiring the strength of four people to move it. It can be considered the largest registry of modern times.

Origin of Dominoes 132

— Wu Achen

Dominoes were once an elegant game, but now they are used for gambling, which goes against the original intention of their creation. Legend has it that dominoes were created during the Xuanhe reign of Emperor Huizong of the Song Dynasty and the Shaoxing reign of Emperor Gaozong. Emperor Gaozong issued an edict to promote their use throughout the land, and the literati of the time regarded studying their various uses as a pastime during their leisure time with poetry and wine. However, they all played alone in bright and clean rooms, unlike modern gamblers who shout and cheer. Although their composition is based on the combinations of twenty-one points and thirty-two cards, their unpredictable variations create endless interest. Although those who play them may be likened to those who build a cart behind closed doors, the resulting mental pleasure surpasses that of entering the market of the Five Capitals. I will now briefly describe what I know:

Belonging to literature, there are card lyrics, card poems, card songs, card tunes, card correspondence, card notes, card letters, card classics, etc. If even one card is incorrect, a complete chain can be formed, unlike the clever combination of five pieces.

Belonging to superstition, there are card divination, card lessons, card tallies, card signs, feng shui cards, fortune-telling cards, treasure-hunting cards, treasure vault cards, judgment cards, dragon-breaking, and the forward, backward, left, and right linking calculation methods specifically for wine, lust, wealth, and anger. There are also so-called tortoise dismantling and sky nine hitting, which are the easiest to perform and are within everyone's capabilities. It is said that the most spiritual divination is the tooth card divine number of Zhuge Liang and the tooth card Bagua of Liu Bowen. If the tooth card divine number is used as the theory, then dominoes already existed in the Han Dynasty, and there was no need to wait for Emperor Gaozong of the Song Dynasty to issue an edict to promote it throughout the land. Such is what I have heard, but whether the tooth card divine number was created by Marquis Wu requires further verification.

Belonging to the humorous, there are cards presenting grievances, cards responding to official documents, cards interrogating confessions, red maiden's card to express love, and Liu's four-door singing, etc. The recently popular card-appearing essay is said to be created by Yuan Suiyuan. The above essays all use the style of points, the amount, the color of the collaboration, and chants with unrestrained and extraordinary four-six sentences. The entire structure can form a chain different from the clever combination of five pieces.

Belonging to emotion, there is Meng Jiangnu searching for her husband for thousands of miles, Madam Sun silently thinking of her husband in Jingzhou, thinking of her husband and shedding tears (commonly known as thinking of ten pairs), Miss E eloping and Qinger patching a hundred na, etc. However, the item coordination is separate from the clever combination of the five pieces, but is only required to form a pair, but still requires thirty-two sheets to be interconnected, but the difference is that there is no linking skill.

Belonging to the martial arts. There are five levels to fight. Guan Gong cuts six generals through five passes. As well as loyal ministers and rebels. Attacking the Tianmen formation and so on. Today's women and children all know that. Only the two kinds of fighting five passes and cutting generals five times and so on are known.

Belonging to art. There are eight auspicious rows of swastika, stacking flower baskets, picking double peaches, and building a road, and finding millet in the sea. The method is simple. There is no difference in relay racing. Only with two or six as the head and three or six as the tail. Yu was poor in the collocation of the number of months. There is still one more thirty-five or twenty-five.

The above-mentioned various uses of the game. Yu in more than ten years. Either through the oral narration of the first kindness. Or through the notes of friends and other friends. Or get in the ancient sages' copy and store it. In the autumn of the fourth year of the Republic of China. Yu was in a second-hand bookstore in Peiping. He once bought five volumes of the copybook of Baifa for a few silver dollars. According to experts, the paper was made in the Ming Dynasty and was supposed to be from the Ming Dynasty. Yu regarded it as an arch wall. Unfortunately, in the spring of the following year. Lost in the outer way. I still regret it.

Recent News from Shantou 133

— Auspicious Post from Shantou

I came to Shantou from Xiamen. It has been more than ten days now. Shantou is more than twice as large as Xiamen, but it may not be as prosperous.

The roads and buildings are fairly flat. Police are visible at all times. However, those who inquire about directions often shake their heads and stare blankly, unsure of what to say. This makes it difficult for newcomers to Shantou. I hope the authorities will provide training.

The number of newspapers is also more than double that of Xiamen. Major newspapers include the Shantou Daily, Lingdong Republican Daily, Xin Lingdong Daily, Chao Mei Xinbao, Minsheng Daily, Tiansheng Daily, Zhenyan Daily, and many others. The layout and arrangement are modeled after Hong Kong newspapers. Among them, the "Shantou Daily" has the widest circulation. "Tiansheng" and "Zhenyan" have a small readership because they have not been published for long. However, the compilation of Tiansheng is still good and is working hard to move forward, not without new opportunities. The compilation and printing of Zhenyan are inferior, and I am afraid it will be difficult to recover on its own. There are three small newspapers: "Shuangri," "Feng," and "Hanjiang." The former comes out every two days, and the latter two appear every three days. The compilation is like a Shanghai small newspaper. The competition is very fierce. Therefore, both the Shuangri and Feng typesetting and printing are excellent. Unfortunately, the city is smaller than Shanghai by an unknown amount. It is not easy to collect information. All newspapers are suspended on Sundays. On Mondays, each newspaper publishes a four-page tabloid-style supplement. It does not talk about politics and society, but only about romance. It is also a new type of separation.

The people of Shantou seem to have a strong love of gambling. Otherwise, how could there be so many treasure platforms that every road must have them. The door plaques all say "Silver Medal". Entering the door is all Fan Tan.

Flowers are divided into "Southern Words", Su Gang, "Provincial Prostitutes", and local "Chao Prostitutes" three types. It is further divided into special, upper, middle, three, lower, and five classes. Depends on the amount of donations they pay. Shantou's donations are so numerous that there is nothing that is not donated. As for

Recreation is far inferior to Xiamen. Theaters are only "Zhenguang", "Guangtian", and "New Stage" three places. There is an "In Time" amusement park in the east, which only provides leisure for the lower class of society. The types of entertainment are also very few. The Shanghai Plum Blossom Dance Troupe once came here to perform for a dozen days. The New Stage was crowded with people and horses, which was very popular for a while. (It is reported that the troupe will leave for Guangzhou on the 17th to perform at the Provincial Education Association) It is good that the people of Shantou often compete to visit when they hear that there are novel songs and dances

What I Heard from Watching a Dance Performance 134

— Wang Qiangcheng

The Shanxi Grand Theater hired the Liang Sisters Dance Troupe to perform various dances starting on May 28th. I had nothing to do on Saturday, so I went to the theater with Mr. Wang Feilong and Mr. Tao Renyan, bought tickets, and entered. A film was already showing. The film was quite profound in its intention and was divided into three segments: (1) death for a woman who pleases; (2) divorce due to money; (3) nearly escaping a disaster for diamonds. It is greatly alarming that the commonplace man and foolish woman of recent times would be obsessed with money. At the end of the film, the dance, Competition of Pearl Dance, was performed. The exquisite posture and beauty can be called unique in Shanghai. It is a pity that the music could not be synchronized, so there were slight regrets. After the first scene was completed, Brother Feilong accompanied me to the backstage. Sai Zhu cried and said that he almost danced wrong today because of the music. A young man raised his voice and said, "I played the piano. Moreover, Ms. So-and-so came to inform us. It was the fault of Ms. So-and-so, not the fault of our music!" After a long argument, it was only after Mr. So-and-so rebuked the young man that it stopped.

News from the Publishing World: Since the closure of the Yi Bao and Jinghua small newspapers in the capital's small newspaper industry, there has been a downturn. Recently, Zhu Zhu Zhan Qiuyun Yong Juexian and others initiated a three-day publication named Xiaoxiao Bao. Most of the writers are well-known figures in Beijing, such as Chen Dabei Zhang Huijian Li Lichen and others. The compilation style is especially unique. It is reported that it has been published on June 1.

Correction: In yesterday's Travels Around the Yellow Sea (21), the station of Odawara Station in the third line was mistaken for a county. This is specially corrected.

New News from the Literary and Artistic World: As the summer heat gradually arrives and fans and leaves are put on the market, Shanghai calligraphers and painters Zhang Yuguang, Wang Zhongshan, Xiong Songquan, Ye Weixin, Gao Shangzhi, Xu Xiaochun, Shen Yizhai, Zhu Wenhou, Wang Yixian, Guo Jilan, Li Lengran, Hong Lisheng and other twelve people are each exhibiting more than 1,000 pages of their favorite folding fans from next Tuesday for three days at the Ningbo Association. At that time, there will also be inexpensive sales of various family painting manuals in order to form a bond with calligraphy and painting. (Snow)

Early Summer Recipe 135

— Ershun

Loquat Balls: Remove the skin and pits of loquats, embed hundred fruits or red bean paste fillings, and make them with candied fruits. Their taste is even better than candied haws.

Lychee Soup: Remove the shells and pits of lychees and cook them with jackfruit in a wok to make a soup.

Waxberry Balls: Take fresh waxberries, remove the pits, dry them in the sun, and mix them with flour and oil. Pan-fry them in a wok until they are golden brown on both sides.

Peach Dumplings: Cut peaches into small pieces, wrap them in red bean paste or walnut and date fillings, wrap a layer of caul fat on the outside, mix them with egg white batter, and put them into a frying pan to fry them into dumplings.

Travels Around the Yellow Sea (23) 136

— Huang Yanpei

One day, I went to visit the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun and received a warm reception from them. As soon as I entered, it was like entering a bookstore. Their printed materials, apart from daily newspapers, were very numerous. There were annual publications such as the Asahi Yearbook, the International League Yearbook, the Sports Yearbook, the Japanese Art Yearbook, the Japanese Photography Yearbook, the Japanese Film Yearbook, the Asahi Economic History, the International Photography Collection, the Asahi Diary for Young Men and Women, Present Day Japan, and other periodicals: Asahi Shimbun Reduced Edition (published on the 5th of each month), Films and Performing Arts Asahi, Children's Asahi (both published on the 1st of each month), Asahi Pictorial, Weekly Asahi (both weekly), Asahi Sports (twice a month). There were correspondence publications, which they called lectures: Asahi Everyday Conversation Lecture, Popular Medicine Lecture, Asahi Public Lecture. There were series of books: Asahi Family Series, Asahi Political and Economic Series, Asahi Sports Series, History of Meiji and Taisho, and various other individual books.

I visited the grand auditorium in the center of their building, which had 1,200 seats for listeners and various facilities for drama, broadcasting, sound recording, and movies. Public lectures and various performances were held there from time to time. There was also an exhibition hall with an area of one hundred square meters.

Their editorial office was equipped with a transmission machine in the air for automatic transmission of documents, which was both quick and labor-saving.

Their printing department had fifteen rotary presses of various types, with a total printing capacity of over 1.36 million sheets per hour.

There was a pigeon house on the roof with over a hundred pigeons. Pigeons were used for communication between Tokyo, Osaka, and Sendai every day. There were fixed devices and methods for how to place and hang the letter on the pigeon's body.

There was a telephoto room. If A and B are far away, if there are activities in A, such as meetings, celebrity travel, and other important activities, the film can be taken from B within 20 minutes and published in the B newspaper using the fastest method.

The entire building had 1,500 people, with rest areas, cafeterias, and public cafeterias attached to the business.

To tell another story, their president, Murayama Ryuhei, was still healthy at a high age and was very persevering and far-sighted. One year, the government ordered the suspension of publication for a few days because he published a certain case, and sales were inevitably affected. He suddenly had a whim and chose a day to have Asahi Shimbun send people to all the trams in the city that day to give away all the fares one by one. As a result, his reputation greatly increased, not only recovering the losses but also gaining extraordinary progress, which was more effective than any advertisement.

I admire the Asahi Shimbun in every way for being able to apply science and scientific methods, and I admire them even more for their far-sightedness, the precision of their organization, and the flexibility of their methods.

A Rotary Club Speech

Occasional Lake Talks (4) 137

— Tianxu I Sheng

People from Hangzhou are good at making allegorical sayings. They often call something large and unexpected "Mu Lao Lao" (Wooden Old Man), without knowing the origin. A guest dining at Wang Runxing's saw someone tell the waiter, "Bring a Mu Lao Lao." At first, he didn't understand what it meant. Soon, a large bowl of fish head tofu was served. The guest, surprised by the abundance, laughed and said, "This is truly a Mu Lao Lao!" Little did he know that the name was actually a riddle. The character "Mu" (wood) hints at "Yu" (fish), and "Lao" (old) covers "Tou" (head) and "Doufu" (tofu). This is similar to the example in the novel *Jing Hua Yuan*, where "Jiang" is used to guess "Ya" (tooth). As for "Ma Qian" (before the horse), it's a hidden phrase of associative meaning. The hidden meaning is just the word "Kuai" (quick, enjoyable). The mutton soup rice at Xile Yuan also often uses riddles. For example, "Feng Tiao Yu" (favorable weather) for "Shen" (kidney) is a homophonic allegorical phrase, and "Liang Dong Er" (bright cave) for "Yan" (eye) is an associative and pictographic phrase. Restaurants also have many hidden phrases. A customer told the waiter, "San Xi Er, don't add Jin Sheng Li," using the character "Jiu" (wine) as a character-splitting riddle and "Shui" (water) as an allegorical saying. Waiters often call new customers "Lai Ma Er," using "Ma" to guess "Ren" (person), and "Er" as a word-assisting particle. Using "Sheng" (sacrifice) as a homophonic allegorical saying for "Sheng" (raw, fresh) is because it's a Hangzhou custom to sacrifice to the God of the Year. Restaurants usually serve a pig's head, eggs, and fish, called "Zhu Tou San Sheng" (pig's head three sacrifices). For ordinary festival sacrifices, pork is used instead of a pig's head, but it's simply called "San Sheng" without mentioning "pig's head." Eggs are used to replace chicken, as *Book of Rites* says, "Scholars and commoners do not kill for no reason." People in Hangzhou often say that the price of goods is surprisingly high, "Qiao Zhu Gan" (knocking bamboo poles), which is also a riddle. It's actually "Ji Tuo" (striking the clapper). The system of "Qiao Bangbang" (knocking the clapper) in Hangzhou involves cutting bamboo into flutes and hanging them on the chest, striking them with bamboo sticks. Every night around the second watch, the sound of the clapper is heard in the streets, called "Qi Geng" (starting the watch). Officials pronounce "Chi" for "Qi" and "Jing" for "Geng," so "Qiao Zhu Gan" is a riddle for "Ji Tuo," and "Qi Geng" is a homophonic allegorical saying for "Chi Jing" (startled), meaning that the high prices are enough to startle people. There's also something called "Pao Wang Gua" (peeling royal cucumber). Royal cucumbers are not valuable items, and people usually eat them with the skin on. Restaurants often prepare them for guests. If a guest asks for it to be peeled into shreds and mixed with sugar and vinegar, the price will be at least eight cents, even though it's only worth a few cents. Therefore, "Pao Wang Gua" is also another name for "selling foreign plates." Some say that when Governors Peng and Zuo were residing on the lake, their officials often wore yellow riding jackets. Whenever they entered a restaurant, they would anxiously call for the waiter, who would rush to serve them and often receive generous rewards. The price was even higher than selling foreign plates, buying "Qian Pan" (money plates). "Dong Yue Ban Diao" (moving and saying half a string) means that half a thousand official coins are worth half a tael of treasury silver, which is even higher than selling foreign plates.

Local News

Wang Chonghui Departs for Europe Today 157

May Meet with Mo Dehui Via Russia; International Court of Justice Rescheduled for July 16th. Dr. Wang Chonghui, President of the Judicial Yuan, has been approved to attend the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague to handle the case of the German-Austrian Customs Union proposed by the Administrative Department of the League of Nations. He will take the Dalian Steamship Company's Tianjin Maru from Shanghai to Dalian at 2:00 PM today. From Dalian, he will take a train through the three northeastern provinces and Soviet Russia to The Hague. The ship is currently docked at the Huangpu Wharf in Yangshupu. When the time comes, Wang will board the ship from there. Wu Kunwu, Counselor of the Judicial Yuan, Zhu Luhe, Minister of Justice, Wei Daoming, Mayor of Nanjing, and Zheng Yuxiu have all arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing and will go to the wharf to see him off. Regarding his whereabouts after leaving Shanghai and the opening of the International Court of Justice, Wang told a New Sound News Agency reporter yesterday, "In addition to having my secretary, Xiao Jin, accompany me to Harbin, I have no one else traveling with me. After arriving in Harbin, I will have to stay for one or two days to wait for the Russian Consulate in Harbin to issue a passport to pass through Russia. Then, I will go west along Siberia to Moscow. If there is an opportunity, I will meet with Mo Dehui, the Plenipotentiary Representative of the Sino-Soviet Conference. However, as far as I know, the train only stops there for two hours, and the train from Siberia is often late. Therefore, it is not yet known whether I will be able to meet with Representative Mo. If the train is not late, there may be a chance; otherwise, I can only pass through there and go directly to Berlin. I have now received a telegram from the International Court of Justice notifying me that the opening date has been changed to the 16th of next month. Therefore, there is still plenty of time on the way. I plan to rest for three or four days in Berlin and then go to The Hague. I expect to arrive at the International Court of Justice by the end of this month, and I plan to return to China at the end of the year."

Mayor of the Capital Wei Daoming, Minister of Justice Zhu Luhe, and others arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing on the morning of the day before yesterday and arrived at the station at 5:00 PM. Because Wang Chonghui was going to The Hague to serve as a judge of the International Court of Justice, Wei and others specially hosted a banquet for Wang at Xinghualou Restaurant on Fourth Avenue at noon yesterday. Xu Weizhen, President of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, Yang Zhaoyun, President of the Local Court, and lawyer Zheng Yuxiu and others accompanied them, offering congratulatory speeches to Wang, saying that Wang's trip to The Hague would not only bring glory to the Chinese judicial community but also allow Europe to understand the situation of the Chinese judicial community. Wang also gave a lengthy response, and the gathering ended happily at 2:00 PM in the afternoon.

Xie Guanying, Secretary of the Judicial Yuan, because the President of the Yuan, Wang Chonghui, was scheduled to depart from Shanghai for Europe today to attend the International Court of Justice, Xie came to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning. He went to Haigen Road in the morning to visit Wang and ask for instructions on all matters of the Yuan.

Chen Shaokuan's Conversation 158

Yongjian and Yongji Will Be Transferred to Fujian and Ningbo

The Central Government Is Eager for Peaceful Resolution of the Guangdong Situation

Guowen News Agency reports that Chen Shaokuan, Naval Vice-Minister and concurrently Director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, came to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning. A Guowen News Agency reporter inquired about the recent naval and Guangdong situation and had a brief conversation as follows: (Q) The Guangdong authorities have rebelled. Will the Navy be dispatched to deal with it? (A) We must only obey the orders of the Central Government. (Q) Then, have orders been received? (A) Not yet. (Q) Since no orders have been received, have there been any preparatory actions? (A) The Guangdong situation is being handled by the Central Government, which is striving for a peaceful resolution. As for preparations, the Navy is very different from the Army. The Navy can depart in five minutes if an incident occurs, so there is no need to prepare. (Q) If there is a need to dispatch to deal with the matter, will the Navy order all naval ships to be transferred south to participate? (A) This matter depends on the extent of the situation. (Q) Is it true that the Yongji and Yongjian ships will first sail to Shantou within the next few days? (A) Yongjian will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow (today). It will sail to Xiamen, Fujian, for patrol within the next few days. Yongji will also be ordered to sail to Xiangshan. It is said that the Datong ship will be transferred to Shanghai, but it is not confirmed that it will sail to Shantou. (Q) When will Minister Yang (Shuzhuang) return to Fujian? (A) The date has not yet been determined. He probably still needs to negotiate financial and political affairs in Fujian in Shanghai. The conversation ended there.

Industrial Zone in This City Has Been Designated and Announced 164

Located North of the Yunzaobang

The number of factories in this city is increasing day by day. The Municipal Works Bureau has designated an industrial zone in the Yunzaobang area for the purpose of implementing the zoning plan. The full text of the announcement is as follows: Announcement: It has been noted that various manufacturing industries in this city are developing rapidly and require considerable open space for the construction of factory buildings. In order to meet the current needs and prepare for the implementation of the city-wide zoning plan, it is proposed to first designate the area north of Yunzaobang as a factory construction site to facilitate development. This plan has been submitted to the Municipal Government and approved in Directive No. 10213, which states that the case has been discussed and decided at the 181st Municipal Government meeting. The area north of Yunzaobang, except for the area within 300 meters along the river, should be reserved, and the rest should be temporarily designated as an industrial zone, etc. It is hereby ordered that the bureau announce it to the public.

More than 600 Western-style bookbinding workers resumed work yesterday. More than 1,200 Chinese-style bookbinding workers are also scheduled to resume work tomorrow. The Party and government organs issued an announcement to suspend union activities and seal up the meeting place to wait for reorganization. The situation yesterday is recorded separately below:

Consultation Method: In order to quickly resolve the issue, Pu Xiejun and Tang Pinji of Pu Fenglai and Tang Apin Bookbinding Shops consulted with Zhang Haosheng, Director of the Union, and Zhang Jinming and Qiao Aken, representatives of the Union, and others in the Wanshang Tea House in Xinzha Bridge yesterday. The results were: (1) Wages for both Chinese and Western-style workers will be increased by 10% uniformly, effective June 1st. (2) The number of apprentices in each Chinese-style workshop will remain the same, limited to five people. (3) The daily meal subsidy for Chinese-style workers will remain the same, at eight cents per worker. However, it must wait until both labor and management and all workers and all colleagues have contacted each other before formally signing the contract at 10:00 AM this morning.

Union Notice: The Bookbinding Union issued Bulletin No. 11 yesterday, stating that the members are not satisfied with the modified treatment conditions, which has led to a labor dispute. Now, the director of the union and ten representatives of the workers have negotiated with the employers on the three items of wage increase, apprenticeship, and meals. The agreement is now more perfect than the previous proposal. It is hereby announced that all workers will resume work uniformly on the 7th of this month. As for the detailed situation, it will be announced after the reorganization is completed. Be sure to do this.

Reorganizing the Union: The Municipal Social Bureau and the Municipal Party Department jointly issued an announcement to suspend union activities and sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau, stating that the current officials of the union are incompetent in leading the current illegal strike of bookbinding workers, and that reorganization is necessary to benefit the labor movement. In addition to jointly announcing with the Municipal Civil Training Association to temporarily suspend the union's activities, we hereby send a letter to the Bureau to ask for instructions to seal up the union's meeting place to facilitate reorganization.

Air Express Mail 172

Extremely Fast in Transfer and Delivery

The Shanghai Postal Authority stated that in order to make the public understand the convenience of air express mail, it will soon issue promotional materials. These promotional materials are specifically for those who purchase airmail stamps and those who send or receive regular airmail. Although regular airmail is relatively fast in transit, according to current regulations, it is delivered at the same time as regular mail. Therefore, if regular airmail arrives at the destination post office after the last delivery time for regular mail, it will inevitably be delayed until the next day for delivery. However, air express mail, even if it arrives at the destination after the last delivery time for regular mail, can be delivered immediately upon arrival. Therefore, for urgent letters, it is best to send them by air express mail, as both transfer and delivery are extremely fast.

Methods for Inspecting and Releasing Exhibits with Bond for Road City Exhibition 173

Ministry of Finance Replies to Road Association

The Road City Exhibition Conference being prepared by the China National Road Construction Association has been scheduled to open on September 12th this year. The exhibits are divided into domestic and foreign categories. In addition to the domestic transportation of exhibits already approved for tax exemption by the Ministry of Finance, the foreign exhibits have now been telegraphed to the Ministry of Finance by the association for approval to handle inspection and release with a bond. The association received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, which briefly stated that the notice of the 22nd and the telegram from President Wang Xun of the National Road Construction Association have been received. The tax deposit paid for the exhibits is a guarantee. If there is no tax deposit, once the goods are inspected and released, there is no way to recover the tax if they are not returned within the time limit. In order to protect tax revenue, the Ministry will still have to handle all exhibits transported by your association uniformly. However, the tax deposit does not necessarily require cash; a bond from a reliable bank can also be used. In addition to instructing the Jianghai Customs Supervisor to instruct the customs commissioner to inspect and release the exhibits transported to your association with a tax deposit and stipulate that they must be returned to their original location within one month after the closing. If they are not returned within the time limit, the tax deposit will not be refunded. If the deposit is a bank bond, the bank providing the bond should be responsible for paying the tax. If the goods returned are less than the goods imported, the tax payable on the missing goods should be deducted from the deposit or paid in full by the bank providing the bond before the original bond can be returned. This special reply is for your information. Finance Minister Song Ziwen, Jiang Yin, discussed and removed the telegram reply to thank and sent telegrams to road city agencies, friendly businesses and commerce groups both domestically and abroad to follow the compliance.

Commodity Inspection Bureau Assists in Inspecting and Transporting Silkworm Eggs on Two Roads 177

From the 5th to the 15th of This Month

Autumn Silkworm Eggs Will Be Exempted from Detention After Identification

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau stated that the summer and autumn silkworm eggs produced by domestic silkworm egg manufacturers are now being transported frequently. They should be detained and released separately. The bureau sent personnel to assist in the inspection at major stations in the silkworm egg areas of the Jinghu and Hangyong railways to facilitate the process. The bureau sent a letter to the management bureaus of the two railways yesterday, requesting them to investigate. The original letter stated: In order to ensure strict inspection and prevent inferior varieties from entering the market, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has requested the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways to instruct the Jianghai Customs and various stations to cooperate in the inspection. However, it has been found that there are many silkworm egg manufacturers in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and the summer and autumn silkworm eggs they produce are transported frequently by land and water. The summer silkworm eggs are already in the sales season and should be detained if they have not been inspected, qualified, and labeled. The autumn silkworm eggs are often transported to cold storage in other cities because the manufacturers do not have cold storage facilities. These silkworm eggs have not been soaked in acid and have not yet reached the reporting period, so they have not been labeled. However, it has been found that autumn silkworm eggs must be sent to cold storage within 24 hours after laying, otherwise the quality will be affected and the loss will be great. It is feared that the inspectors at various stations will detain them all without distinguishing between them, causing danger. However, it is not easy for non-silkworm experts to distinguish between summer and autumn eggs. In order to facilitate inspection, the bureau will assign one or two technicians to assist in the inspection at various stations in the silkworm egg areas of Shanghai, Suzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, Nanjing, and Hangzhou from the 5th to the 15th of this month to facilitate the process. After the deadline, the silkworm eggs that have not been labeled will still be detained according to the previous regulations. In addition to sending letters to various stations, this letter is sent to your bureau for investigation.

The Case of the Drunken Cook of the American Ship Is Closed 178

A Glimpse of the Chinese People's Love of Peace

The Municipal Public Security Bureau sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, stating: On the afternoon of May 27, the merchant ship Atlan City, managed by the American Steel Company, was docked at the Qichangzhan Pier in Pudong, this city. A cook named A. Tanarelis Tiff (transliteration) disembarked from the pier and, being heavily intoxicated, staggered into the town's main street, running wildly. At that time, many pier workers were leaving a restaurant after eating. The cook ran into them, brandishing a small fruit knife as if to stab them. Yang Jin'er, Wang Jinfa, Ma Lin, and others were unable to avoid him. Yang's right thigh was stabbed, Ma's left cheek was slightly scratched, and Wang's right eye was punched. The Third District Police Station was reported and immediately dispatched a senior police officer to the scene to stop the cook, who fled back to the ship. The ship's captain used a rope to tie him up and expressed his responsibility to punish the cook. Chief Patrolman Shen returned to the station and reported the incident by telephone to the Third District, which was forwarded to this bureau by District Chief Zhang. After investigation, on the morning of the 29th, the ship's captain sent a letter of apology to the Third District, stating that he was deeply grateful that the senior police officer had arrived at the scene and made every effort to maintain order, avoiding other unexpected accidents. He also expressed his deep apologies and was willing to compensate the injured for medical expenses of 20 yuan and be punished in accordance with the Law on Violations of Public Security. Subsequently, the injured parties stated in the district that their injuries were extremely minor and that they did not wish to file a lawsuit, and a settlement was filed. The Third District fined the cook 10 yuan. Chen Zhiliang, the secretary of the papermaking workers' union, who did not know the truth, distributed printed flyers. The bureau summoned Chen and the injured parties, Yang Jin'er and Ma Lin, to the bureau for questioning. Their statements were consistent with what they had said in the district. The bureau distributed the medical expenses paid by the cook, with Yang Jin'er receiving 14 yuan and Wang Jinfa and Ma Lin receiving 3 yuan each. A statement was drawn up and the case was closed. Chen Zhiliang also realized that the flyers he had issued were not consistent with the facts and that there had been a misunderstanding. He was very sorry. The bureau did not pursue the matter further as he had admitted his mistake. This case involves an American merchant ship's cook who, while drunk, assaulted passersby. The reports in various newspapers were mostly mistaken by reporters, which were exaggerated and misleading. This special letter is sent to clarify the facts.

Lu Zhongen and Lu Dongsheng Sever Their Adoptive Father-Son Relationship 185

Allowance of 800 Dollars

No Longer Father and Son

Lu Zhongen was originally the illegitimate son of Lu Zizhuang and Hua Shen, when Zizhuang was a pastor in Songjiang. When he was nine years old, Zizhuang handed him over to his younger brother, Dongsheng, to be raised as an adopted son. Later, Hua Shen requested that Lu Zhongen provide some support, but he refused, leading to a lawsuit. Dongsheng also sued the Special Zone Court for severing the adoptive relationship, citing Zhongen's violent temperament and other reasons. The preliminary judgment rejected his claim. The original claim and the main points are summarized as follows: The plaintiff adopted Hua Zhongen as his adopted son in 1916, when he was only nine years old. He raised, educated, and found him a job, and he married this year. However, the defendant did not follow the teachings, kicked his adoptive mother, beat his niece, and denied his biological mother's request for support in court, which shows that his nature has been destroyed and he has no conscience. Therefore, he requests to sever the relationship. The defendant responded that the plaintiff is his adoptive father and his biological father, Lu Zizhuang, is his biological father. When he was a pastor in Songjiang, he had a relationship with the defendant's biological mother, Hua Shen, and had the defendant. He was adopted by the plaintiff. His original wife, Zhao, loved the defendant more than her own son, and the defendant also regarded her as his own parents. Zhao even cut her flesh to cure her relatives when she was ill. However, after Zhao's death, the scene changed greatly when his stepmother, Wang, came to the house, and his adoptive father also changed slightly. Now, he falsely accuses the defendant of being a child of a different surname and requests to sever the adoptive relationship. He has already filed another lawsuit to confirm his identity. The reasons for the judgment are summarized as follows: The plaintiff's claim that the defendant is usually violent cannot be supported by evidence. As for the claim that he does not recognize his biological mother, which shows that his nature has been destroyed, the defendant claimed that he did not not recognize her, but that he did not know her. The defendant has been raised by the plaintiff since he was a child and has not heard from his biological mother for a long time. It is true that he does not know who his mother is, and it is difficult to say that this is a complete lack of conscience. It is difficult to justify the request to sever the relationship with an adopted son who has been raised for more than ten years. Later, Lu Dongsheng refused to accept the original judgment and hired lawyer Wen Chao to appeal to the Higher Second Branch Court. Yesterday was the opening date for the trial. Judge Hu Yigu presided over the trial. He first said that Lu Zhizhuang was ill and did not come today, and the witnesses were not all present. However, the case should be settled amicably. He then told Lu Dongsheng that when you adopted this child, he was only nine years old. Raising him until now must have cost you a lot of effort and money. Moreover, you married him off last year, which shows that your original purpose was to have him support you in your old age and live peacefully. Now, unfortunately, you have disagreements and request to sever the relationship. His productive capacity is still weak. He only earns 25 yuan a month in the Engineering Bureau. It is difficult to support a family under such circumstances. It is better to give him some money according to my suggestion and order him to live separately. If your son can change his temperament due to the external environment and think that there is still room for reconciliation, then the father and son can reunite. If he still does not change his temperament, then they will be separated permanently and will no longer interact with each other. Moreover, you have already spent a lot of money on his education and marriage. This is the last time you will be kind to him. People are not grass and trees, and they will always be grateful and repay you one day. At first, Lu Dongsheng only agreed to give 100 yuan. Later, after the judge repeatedly persuaded him, he agreed to give 600 yuan. Lu Zhongen claimed that his income was not high, which made it difficult for him to live. If he could give him 1,000 yuan and deposit it in the bank, he would only take the interest and not move the principal to subsidize his household expenses. Moreover, he had no ill feelings towards his adoptive father. If his productive capacity increased in the future, he would not only not want the allowance, but he would also be willing to learn from the filial crows to give back. The judge then summoned Lu Wang and told him that you can persuade your husband to give a little more allowance to settle this matter. After several parties, including the lawyer, discussed it, Lu Dongsheng was ordered to pay 800 yuan in foreign currency in three months. After Zhongen received the money, he moved out the belongings and was not allowed to pester his adoptive father. It is hoped that the father will change his mind and the son will reform himself in order to reunite in the future. The case was thus concluded.

The Luoyang Maru Collides With the Pier 187

Five Tugboats Forced to Drag Her Out

Two Tugboats Collide With Each Other and Are Damaged

The Luoyang Maru, a Yangtze River ship of the Nissin Shipping Company, was docked for repairs this time, and the work was completed yesterday afternoon. The company sent a small steamship, the Anshan Maru, to Pudong to tow the Luoyang Maru to the Nissin Pier in Hongkou to load goods for Hankou. At about 2:00 PM, when the Luoyang Maru arrived at the Waibaidu Bridge, it was hit by the tide, and the ship's left side violently collided with the wooden pier outside the pier. The ship was immediately stuck and could not move. The small Anshan Maru went forward to tow it, but it was ineffective.

Four Tugboats Were Called for Rescue

The Anshan Maru was unable to tow the ship and urgently reported to the Nissin General Office. The Kunshan Maru and Jidao Maru tugboats were dispatched to help. At about 2:30 PM, the two tugboats towed together, but it was useless. The ship reported to the General Office again, and the company dispatched its number one powerful tugboats, the Bai Maru and Shan Maru, to continue to assist in the rescue. At that time, it was about 3:00 PM, and the four tugboats towed together, but it was still useless.

The Small Ships Collided and Damaged

The Bai Maru and Shan Maru tugboats were unable to tow the ship, so they changed their strategy. The Bai Maru joined a steel cable to try to drag the Luoyang Maru horizontally, and two tugboats were dispatched to escort it from behind, which would be easier. Unexpectedly, when the Bai Maru turned its ship, its bow and the bow of the Shan Maru were in a straight line and could not avoid each other. The two tugboats collided with each other, and the hulls of the Bai Maru and Shan Maru were damaged, and the iron poles on the ships were also damaged, resulting in huge losses. The pier was damaged. At about 4:00 PM, the Luoyang Maru was finally pulled out by the full force of the four small ships. The wooden pier outside the pier was damaged by the hull of the Luoyang Maru. The steel plate of the Luoyang Maru's own hull was not severely damaged, but the damage to the pier was quite large. After the Luoyang Maru was pulled out, it immediately loaded goods and left. The damaged small ship pier needs to be repaired today.

Dogs Must Be Registered and Licensed 188

The Municipal Health Bureau Prevents the Harm of Mad Dogs

In order to prevent the harm of mad dogs and protect the safety of citizens, the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau has formulated measures to ban stray dogs and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval. All dog owners in the Shanghai Municipal District, whether officials or civilians, should apply for a license in accordance with the regulations of the bureau and pay a license fee of 50 cents per dog. Dog owners in the rural areas of the city should apply for registration at the health offices in their respective districts and pay a fee of 25 cents per dog. Dog owners who delay or violate the regulations will be punished. Subsequently, a new license should be renewed once every January. The bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that all dog owners must report their dogs in order to avoid stray dogs and domestic dogs being mistaken. Many dog owners in the city have already registered, but many have not yet obtained a license.

Please send the samples of your products for display. This is a good opportunity to promote national products, so do not miss it. Continuing Records of Contraband Seized by Customs 191

The Jianghai Customs seized a large quantity of drugs, 392 pounds of heroin, from the Dutch ship "Kimi" of the Java Company, and also seized 179 pounds of heroin from the Japanese ship "Dou Beng Maru," as reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the Dutch ship "Kimi" came to Shanghai from Germany and the Netherlands, and customs officials were dispatched to search the ship because they had received a secret report in advance. The search of the Japanese ship took place at the Merchants' Wharf. Both batches of drugs were shipped from Germany. It was confirmed yesterday that when the large quantities of drugs carried by the two ships this time were shipped out of Europe, no one except the parties involved knew about the procedures, which were very secret. It is not known whether the ship's employees and owners were aware of this, otherwise, such valuable items would not have been transported without incident. Furthermore, since there was no consignee, it is still unknown who purchased and transported the goods. After the Dutch ship had its cargo confiscated, the shipping bureau and the ship are not responsible. Therefore, the ship has already sailed. However, after detailed investigation, it was found that some of the drugs on the Dutch ship may have been transshipped to Vladivostok via Shanghai, and some of the drugs on the Japanese ship may have been transshipped to North China and Dalian. Now that they have all been confiscated, the shipping bureau is still thoroughly investigating the shipping company in order to identify the person who privately loaded the goods, so as to know the location of the principal and the name of the company.

Western Police Unprovoked Abuse of Chinese 192

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to the Municipal Council, Warning

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday regarding the case of Western police officers abusing Chinese people without provocation. The letter stated: "Respectfully, according to a letter from Mr. Yuan Yiqing, on the evening of May 30th, when the singer Hong Mudan performed at the Broadway Theater in Tilanqiao, the iron gates were tightly closed in advance. The audience waited at the corner of the road until nearly 8:45 pm when a small hole was opened, allowing only one person to enter in a stooped position. The theater also hired Western police officer No. 140 and two Chinese police officers as if facing a formidable enemy. At that time, a fellow Chinese citizen, for some unknown reason, angered the Western police officer and was brutally beaten. Not only was he beaten, but he was also taken to the police station. Many fellow citizens witnessed this and were outraged, demanding refunds for their tickets. The duty of the police is to maintain order. If there is no disturbance of the peace, how can they arbitrarily detain people? At that time, I personally witnessed that the person in question did not resist and was a law-abiding citizen. Therefore, the actions of the Western police officer were illegal. The honor and disgrace of one person is a small matter, but the entire personality of us Chinese is a big matter. Moreover, it is the sixth anniversary of the May 30th Incident, and foreigners have no regard for insulting us as before. If the crowd had resisted due to temporary anger, wouldn't the tragedy of the May 30th Incident be reenacted at that time? Therefore, we request your council to seriously negotiate with the Municipal Council in accordance with the law to prevent such unfortunate incidents from recurring in the future." The association believes that Western police officers often abuse their authority and insult residents, which is likely to cause unfortunate incidents. According to the aforementioned letter, we request your council to pay special attention to this matter and investigate the Western police officer concerned.

Li Zuoming Sentenced for Privately Making Post Office Receipts 193

Sentenced to Three Years and Six Months in Prison

Li Zuoming, a staff member of the closed post office and a native of Ningbo, privately made post office customs receipts outside the office. He colluded with Xu Linxiang, Zhou Weiming, and others to defraud customs duties and postage under the pretext of mailing packages for shops, and the money was divided among them for personal use. The police successively arrested them, and together with the suspect Shui Quanxiang, they were handed over to the Special District Local Court for interrogation. The details were reported previously. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao continued the trial and concluded the case. Li Zuoming was sentenced to three years and six months in prison, Xu and Zhou were each sentenced to one year in prison with a three-year suspended sentence, and Shui Quanxiang was acquitted. The counterfeit receipts were confiscated.

Two Key Culprits in Three Kidnapping Cases Each Sentenced to Five Years 194

The kidnapping bandits Zhang Debiao and Hao Zifeng successively conspired with gangs this year to kidnap Wang Zhenhuan, the young owner of Wang Yutai on Julaida Road in the French Concession, Zhu Ligeng, a silk merchant at 215 Changsha Road in the Public Concession, and Ding Ziren, the manager of Fuxin Flour Factory, etc. Afterwards, the police cracked the cases and arrested many kidnappers, who were separately handed over for trial. The details have been reported previously. However, the two bandits Zhang and Hao escaped and remained at large. The authorities issued arrest warrants. Detectives of the French Concession, Supervisor Jin Jiu, Detective Li Yaolong, Deputy Detectives Qian Yumin, Mao Jingen, Zhang Ziying, and Detectives Zhou Buguang and Qin Youyu, etc., learned that Zhang was hiding in Room 7 of the Dongchang Inn in Wufengli, Xiafei Road, and Hao was hiding at No. 26 Jipingli, Wangzhi Road. They went to the addresses without making a sound the day before yesterday and arrested the two bandits, Zhang and Hao, and confiscated a box cannon, along with the bandits' wives, Zhang Sunshi and Hao Sishi, etc., and took them to the police station for custody. Yesterday, they were sent to the French Court for trial. The Western detective first reported the previous situation. Zhang and Hao confessed to conspiring to kidnap the plaintiffs. Sunshi and Sishi also confessed that they had been acquainted with Zhang and Hao for a short time. Zhang, etc., instructed the women to carry pistols, but they did not know about the kidnapping. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced the two bandits Zhang and Hao to five years in Western prison and deportation, and sent them to the inland court for trial. They were first sent to the Public Concession Police Station to investigate the case. The confiscated box cannon was confiscated.

Ye Mingshan Sentenced to Life Imprisonment

Qu and Xue Sentenced to Twelve Years

Jin Anxiang, a runner of the Minfeng Paper Company on the Museum Road, was kidnapped by bandits in front of the doctor Song Boqui's door in Renheli, Baike Road, on the morning of April 22nd. Except for Chen Jinsheng, who died of illness shortly afterwards, the remaining three, Ye Mingshan, Qu Qingxiang, and Xue Zhaofu, have been tried and concluded by the Special District Local Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge opened the court and ordered the bandits to be brought to the court for sentencing. Ye Mingshan was sentenced to life imprisonment and deprived of his political rights for life. Qu and Xue were each sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment and deprived of their political rights for twelve years. Three pistols, one hundred and two bullets, three magazines, ransom letters, and drafts of letters, etc., were confiscated. In addition, the three rooms of Qu's house located in the Yangxing Township, Thirty-One Map, Lishan County, belonging to Qu Qingxiang, were also confiscated.

A Woman Fell and Was Injured Due to a Broken Staircase in Pinjili 196

Due to Not Being Repaired for More Than Ten Years

The houses in Pinjili, Wengjia Branch Lane, Jinjiafang, West Gate of this port, were rebuilt in the seventh year of the Republic of China. At that time, the construction cost was extremely cheap. The construction was handled by a Mr. Pan, and the structure of the house was quite strong. The structure of the sun deck was very simple. The handrail of the sun deck was made of foreign pine planks, which were installed next to the sun deck. They were exposed to the sun and rain, and were invaded day and night. In addition, they had not been repaired for many years, resulting in the wooden stairs being moldy and unusable. Unexpectedly, at about 6 pm yesterday, a woman from the Teng family at No. 15 in the lane went to the sun deck to collect clothes. When she stepped on the handrail, it suddenly collapsed, and the woman fell with the stairs, injuring her head and arms. She was covered in blood and fainted instantly, losing consciousness. After waking up, her senses were abnormal. Her internal injuries were also quite serious. It is said that the injured person was sent to the hospital for treatment. According to the tenants, the landlord has not repaired the house even once in more than ten years, causing this disaster.

Woman Took Poison in Regret After Losing Her Footing 197

Wu Suying, a 19-year-old woman from Huzhou, lost her father at a young age and was raised by her mother. However, the family's finances declined and life was difficult. Unfortunately, in August of last year, according to the old calendar, she was brought to Shanghai by her mother. Through the introduction of a friend from her hometown, she became a prostitute at the Yihong Ya'er brothel at the Dongxin Bridge in the French Concession to earn a living. Fu Yiming, a clerk from a Yuxiaozhen hotel on Yangxing Street, happened to be the same age as Wu. After they got to know each other, their feelings grew day by day. After a long time, they secretly made a lifelong commitment. Unexpectedly, this matter was discovered by her mother, who interfered and sabotaged it again and again. The two had no choice but to agree to wait for an opportunity. Until a week ago, her mother suddenly returned to her hometown due to an incident. The two took this opportunity to elope and temporarily hid in Room 7 of the Central Hotel in Xiaodongmen. After nearly ten days, Suying recently heard that her mother would return to Shanghai in a day or two. Knowing that she would not have a good outcome at that time, she deeply regretted everything she had done rashly. After repeated consideration, she was filled with worry and indignation. At about 4 pm yesterday, while Fu was out, she secretly bought a large amount of opium and swallowed it. Fortunately, the tea room attendant caught a glimpse of it and immediately reported the situation to the Yi Section Chief of the Second Branch of the First District. After hearing the report, the section chief immediately sent a patrol officer to rush to the scene and send Wu to Shanghai Hospital for treatment in a car. It is reported that the toxicity has not yet erupted and her life can be saved.

Appeal for Disaster Relief in Rehe 199

The Chinese Red Cross Society recently received a joint telegram from Zhou Tiezheng, the magistrate of Chaoyang County, Rehe, the heads of various bureaus of the county government, Meng Fubin, the president of the Chaoyang Red Cross Society branch, and the leaders of organizations, stating: "The mountains in the third district of Chaoyang are rugged, the people are poor, and the land is barren. If the rain falls in time, the harvested grain is only enough to make a living. If disasters occur frequently, the villagers have no way to survive. This is the actual situation in this area, which should be known to those who have lived in this land. Last year, continuous rain caused a disaster. The river water rose and flooded the fertile fields at the foot of the mountains. Some were completely washed away, turning good fields into riverbeds. Some were flooded and became barren, turning fertile land into sand. As a result, those who were well-off in the morning became destitute in the evening. As for the fields in the mountains, the rainwater has been continuous, and the soil has become even more barren, with very little harvest. Since the beginning of winter last year, the money supply has been extremely tight and the price of grain has been low. Knowing that there is a shortage of food, they still have to sell it to repay debts. It is like cutting the flesh from the heart to treat the current wound. It is indeed unavoidable. This spring, borrowing money is impossible. How can there be a way to turn stone into gold? As a result, those who carry their children and daughters and flee for their lives are everywhere, and nine out of ten households are starving. The buds of trees and wild vegetables have been completely dug up. The suffering of displacement is indescribable. Representatives cannot bear to sit idly by and are unable to lend a hand. They can only sigh and lament. We have always admired the great philanthropists who are concerned about the suffering of the people and have the spirit of universal relief and the ability to do everything. They will rescue those in need, regardless of distance or relationship. They are moved by the sight of misery and touched by the sound of disaster. We beg you to extend your grace and save the people in the entire area. We beg you to have great compassion and revive the dying fish in the drying rut. Not only will the disaster victims in the entire area be grateful for your rebirth, but the representatives will also never forget your mercy. We are eagerly looking forward to your reply."

Publication of Chicken Raising to Begin Pre-Orders 218

Chicken Raising is written by Mr. Wang Zhaotai, China's first expert in improving chicken breeds. Mr. Wang has served as the director of chicken farms at famous universities in China and is currently the director of the Seed Chicken Breeding Farm of the Dingxian Plain People's Education Association in Hebei. The book is based on his experience of more than ten years and is compiled using scientific methods suitable for the latest situation in China. It contains detailed discussions on incubation, chicken raising, feeding, breeding, disease, the world's chicken raising situation, and chicken house construction. In particular, the explanation of the methods of improving chicken breeds and promotion is even more detailed. The whole book has more than 200,000 words and more than 100 illustrations, totaling more than 400 pages. It is made of Western-style exquisite hard-shell cloth covers. The price is 3 yuan per copy and will be published at the end of July. It is issued by the North China Seed Chicken Association at No. 61 Xizhimen Street, Beiping. Pre-orders will begin from now until the end of July. Those who go to subscribe during this period will get a 20% discount. Out-of-town residents must add 20 cents for postage. If the exchange is not possible, they can also use postage stamps (limited to 1 cent to 10 cents) at a 95% discount. Those who pre-order more than 10 copies can get a 30% discount. According to Mr. Wang, if the Chinese people can completely follow the methods in the book to improve chicken raising, the number of additional income increased in the country within one year will be more than ten thousand. This book can be used as a reference for both public agricultural organizations and private researchers who improve chicken breeds, or as a textbook for agricultural schools. It is especially suitable for those who are interested in promoting chicken raising and solving the people's livelihood problems. The North China Seed Chicken Association also has various European and American machines and famous chicken breeds, and has branch farms in Jinan Xinyao, Shijiazhuang Suzhou, and Anguo for consultation from all walks of life. In addition, the association also has a chicken raising correspondence school that has recently begun to enroll students. Those who wish to request detailed information can attach a 5-cent stamp and it will be sent.

A resolution was made to approve the filing. The Stevedores' Union held its 79th regular meeting yesterday. Chairman Chen Haiqiu performed the rituals. (2) Regarding the location of the inaugural meeting, a resolution was made to hold it at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association. (4) (5) Omitted. The Fifth District Cigarette Industry Workers' Union issued a declaration to support the workers of the British-American Tobacco Factory in Hankou (omitted above). Recently, the workers of the British-American Tobacco Factory in Hankou demanded payment for the May 5th Commemoration Day holiday and two and a half months of rice subsidies. The factory not only refused but also automatically shut down the factory as a threat, causing the livelihood of thousands of workers to be cut off. Workers must not strike without authorization, and factories must not shut down without authorization. The Chinese government has repeatedly emphasized this. Although they are foreign capitalists, they should absolutely abide by it. Moreover, the payment of wages for holidays on revolutionary memorial days has long been clearly stipulated. How can they violate it? Our association shares the joys and sorrows of the factory workers. Upon hearing the news, we are filled with grief and indignation. We uphold the principle of mutual assistance and pledge to face any difficulty with unwavering resolve. We hope that the factory workers will be unyielding and fight to the end for the May 5th Revolution, even if it means death with honor. We will use justice to resist power and surely prevail. We also hope that the municipal government authorities will strictly abide by the late Premier's teachings on protecting the interests of laborers and strive to maintain them, leading the masses forward. The future of the labor movement depends on it. This declaration is hereby made.
