Weather Report 221

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday: Hot weather with dust. There will be thunderstorms in the watershed. The wind above the East China Sea is from the east to southeast, regardless of the mountain. The wind along the Shandong coast is from the south to southwest. The cyclone between Taiwan and Luzon is intensifying, indicating the formation of a low-pressure area. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 84.9 degrees, and the lowest was 64.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 81.7 degrees, and the lowest was 63.5 degrees.

Letter to the Editor 222

Your newspaper's 30th issue carried a news item titled "Xiong Yimin's Body Divided into Two Sections." It stated that Xiong (Yimin) went to the Law School in the morning to meet his cousin and did not return to his residence until after 11:00 PM. He was unexpectedly run over and killed by the last train coming from the North Station while crossing the tracks. This is inconsistent with the facts. According to my uncle, Yimin left the Law School on the morning of the 28th to handle important matters. At around 10:00 PM, patrol officers of the Songhu Railway Police discovered a male corpse in front of the Law School that had been run over into two sections by a train. Upon hearing the news, students from the Law School rushed to the scene. My uncle, Qingyun, recognized the body as that of my uncle, Yimin. The exact time he was run over by the train is still unknown. This is a correction. I hope you will publish it. Xiong Qingquan, Nanjing.

To the Editor: I am writing in response to a news item in your newspaper's local news section on June 5th regarding a lawsuit against the manager and partners of the Huizhong Bank. I am very surprised. I am writing to provide your newspaper with the true facts and request a correction. The manager of the Sanyou Tobacco Factory at 218 Yalu Road, Fan Songling, used the entire machinery of the factory as collateral to borrow money from our company, with the Qianyuan Tobacco Factory and the Liangzhou Tobacco Factory as guarantors. When the loan was being negotiated, the Sanyou Tobacco Factory had already been seized and sealed by the court due to debts. The borrowed money was used to redeem and unseal the factory. Shortly after, the guarantors came to our company and reported that the Sanyou Tobacco Factory had recently accumulated heavy debts and would inevitably repeat its previous mistake. Based on this information, our company reviewed its accounts and discovered that the debts were overdue and unpaid. We immediately sent a letter to the factory urging them to repay the debts as soon as possible within five days. Unexpectedly, they ignored it. On the afternoon of May 18th, we sent two foreign staff members to demand payment. Who knew that the factory would falsely claim to be closed and refuse entry? The foreign staff members returned and reported this. We then sent two coppersmiths familiar with machinery to inspect the machines. After they left, Fan Songling immediately ordered the doors to be closed and launched an attack on our staff, causing them to suffer humiliation and return injured. We reported this to the Hongkou Police Station at the time. The police station sent detectives to investigate, and the injured were sent to the Red Cross Hospital with injury certificates. In addition to formally filing a lawsuit in court requesting a fair trial, we are requesting a prompt correction to clarify the matter and dispel confusion. I eagerly await this. Sincerely, Huizhong Bank, June 5th, Special Delivery, To the Editor-in-Chief of Shenbao.

My Views on Labor 223

(Continued) Huang Fu

Speech at the Labor University

As mentioned above, the meaning that the universe gives to life is labor. Therefore, labor can be called humanity's vocation. Then, if everyone fulfills their respective labor responsibilities to complete their vocation, how can there be a distinction between labor classes in society? Not only did ancient China have the principle of equality among the four classes (scholars, farmers, artisans, and merchants), but Guanzi also stated that the four classes are the foundation of the state, and the state cannot stand without any one of them. Even in European and American history, there was no record of a labor problem until a century and a half ago. The reason why the labor problem is so prevalent today is due to the Industrial Revolution in the distant past and the European War in the recent past. Since the Industrial Revolution, the production mechanism has expanded, and the quantity of production has increased dramatically. At the same time, in order to improve and refine, various countries have encouraged various inventions and stipulated various patent rights in law. As a result, the gap between the rich and the poor in society has widened. By the time the European War ended and the peace conference began, there was a proposal for an International Labor Organization among various countries. At that time, we thought that the Paris Peace Conference was a meeting for the Allied powers to negotiate peace with Germany. Discussions on reparations, territorial concessions, arms limitations, and war responsibilities were all appropriate topics. However, labor protection regulations were a matter of internal affairs and had no connection to the war against Germany. Why should it be proposed at the peace conference and included in the peace treaty? Only after careful investigation did we realize that there was a deeper meaning behind this. After the war ended, the armies that had expanded excessively during the war would inevitably be demobilized. The military supply factories and other war-related businesses that were busiest during the war also declined sharply. For a time, there was an oversupply of labor, and there was no way to find employment for them. The original positions in ordinary industries before the war were mostly occupied by female workers, and their performance was good, so it was impossible to deprive them of their livelihoods. Therefore, in the name of protecting labor, they advocated reducing working hours. For example, those who previously adopted a twelve-hour system now switched to an eight-hour system, which reduced their productivity by one-third. If a certain factory maintained its original production volume, it would inevitably have to hire one-third more workers according to its original total number of employees. This would not only allow the country to accommodate a large portion of the surplus labor, but also, in theory, while reducing working hours, wages should naturally be reduced proportionally. However, during the war, prices soared, and the cost of living increased significantly. It was difficult to maintain the old wages, let alone reduce them. They even had to discuss increasing them. At the same time, the Russian regime was controlled by the Communist Party, and the voice of preferential treatment for workers was rising high (in fact, in present-day Russia, in order to complete the five-year industrial plan, they are working tirelessly day and night under compulsion, and there is no preferential treatment to speak of). A slight mishandling of the situation would lead to extremism. Therefore, there were also proposals to improve factory treatment and increase wages. This is another meaning. Although reducing working hours, improving factory treatment, and increasing wages all reduce productivity and increase production costs, they are extremely unfavorable to international commercial warfare policies after the war. For example, if there are two factories, A and B, with the same nature, scale, organization, and number of employees, the factory in country A works twelve hours a day, and the daily wage per person is four yuan. The factory in country B works eight hours a day, and the wage is eight yuan. Moreover, factory A does not need to have facilities such as bathrooms, cafeterias, and entertainment venues to fix part of its capital, while factory B does. In this case, if the goods produced by the two factories are equally exquisite, the production cost of factory B will inevitably be several times higher than that of factory A. How can they cope with the commercial warfare that follows? Therefore, the European and American labor problem has transformed into an international labor problem. They must ensure that all countries in the world, regardless of wages, time, and treatment, are unified under a single agreement and follow the same path. This way, in theory, the productivity per person per day will be equal, and the production cost per factory per product will also be equal. Only then, in the commercial warfare arena, will those with strong capital, deep experience, abundant raw materials, excellent worker productivity, and complete financial transportation institutions win, or else they will lose. This is the inevitable trend. This is the fundamental meaning of the establishment of the International Labor Organization by European and American powers. We should see through the inside story and examine how our country's capital is (Mr. Sun Yat-sen said that there is no such thing as wealth in our country, only great poverty and small poverty. Alas, this is a painful statement). How is our experience and raw materials? How is the productivity of our workers and our financial transportation institutions? Alas, we can know what to strive for.

Social News

The Most Glorious Page of the Emden (Continued) 224

— Lin

Miracles of Nature

Now everyone, imagine on a remote island in the Indian Ocean, amidst the jungle on a white sand beach, there is a snow-white seabird spreading its wings to protect its chicks from the scorching sun. The one treating it well is a so-called white man, covered in wounds and stained yellow by ammunition. He is half-crazed with thirst. This person only needs to lift a hand to get forty pounds of fresh meat, but I cannot do that because her eyes are fixed on me, revealing a firm look. I have forgotten the surrounding environment, only feeling the strangeness of life.

Later, I searched in the woods and encountered a group of seagulls that had grown up but had not yet grown feathers. They were next to a tributary. When I walked past them, they called out to me for food. This really stunned me. I picked up the biggest one, wanting to tear off his head, but I couldn't do it. His head and neck twisted like a rubber band and sprang back repeatedly. Later, I bit off his head and sucked his blood. The taste was terrible.

When I was a child, I admired Robinson Crusoe, but the current environment is beyond my expectations. For example, I have never read in a book that there are thousands of small insects on the white sand beach ready to suck human blood. At night, when our energy is restored, everyone goes to the Schnee warship, otherwise, they will become victims of small insects or man-eating birds. As for whether we can invite mercy, it is still unknown. Therefore, twelve of us boarded an old and unsuitable for navigation lifeboat and sailed into the raging sea. But we tried our best to move the boat forward, but we were pushed back by the big waves. The heavy boat was very difficult to move.

After two hours, everyone was exhausted. Of the twelve people on the boat, only three were left. The other nine were knocked to the bottom of the boat by the huge waves. The remaining people tried hard to row the boat towards the bay, where the waves were as high as mountains and hit our necks. Apart from exerting our last strength, we prayed to heaven. When we set off, there were eight oars on the boat. Now, except for just one, they have all been washed into the sea. We had to rely on this one oar to slowly and unstably row forward desperately. Apart from pushing the land backward, I have never been more joyful.

Escaping Death

Suddenly the lifeboat leaked and immediately flooded. Before the boat was smashed to pieces, we tried our best to row towards the distant Schnee. Two people bailed out the water in the boat, and the third person rowed desperately to get closer to the big ship. At first, we could not see the ladder of the Schnee, even though it was lit with lights. In the moonlight, we often saw groups of sharks circling our small boat. The boat often made creaking noises, indicating that it could no longer withstand the impact of the huge waves.

Finally, our small boat approached the ladder of the Schnee. Because it was my turn to row at this time, I was the last person to step onto the solid ladder. When one foot was on the ladder, I felt the small boat sink downwards. When the other foot was raised, only a few pieces of broken wood were floating on the water, and many disappointed sharks were also startled on the water.

The officers on the Schnee warship shone the lights on us and immediately searched us. This was really an easy task because our clothes were long gone. What I can't forget the most is the cup of tea they gave us, the taste of which was indescribably good.

Later, we were transferred to a French cruiser and transported to Colombo. We squeezed in a small passage under the ladder. We had no clothes and no blankets and suffered the pain of prisoners of war. Several British soldiers on the ship sent food and blankets to us, but the French soldiers standing on the ladder strongly refused. There were three times when our friends pushed the French soldiers down the ladder and then sent the blankets and food to us, but in this way, they were not allowed to go up the ladder to see us.

In my opinion, this kind of treatment of prisoners of war is really unfair. If prisoners of war fell into our hands, the situation would be very different. In Penang, the Emden sank a French destroyer. Our captain, Molo, lowered the boat to rescue thirty-six French soldiers before the enemy's artillery fire was over. Although there was very little food and cigarettes on board, we still shared them with them. When we transported them to another ship, they all shouted thanks. They also said that they had heard people say that the Germans treated prisoners of war very cruelly.

We were transferred to the Helmsqua ship and sent to Malta. I would like to say that there are very few of us who survived from the Emden, only about fifty people. After the war, I met a few of them, but everyone's appearance was different from before. The Cocos Islands battle was really fatal.

Leisurely Journey

This is a historical event. The forty-nine people who were left on the island sailed an old Aijixia sailboat with a little food and fresh water towards the Arabian coast. When they arrived there, everyone went ashore and took a car through the desert to Damascus, but their clothes were tattered and their faces were haggard, and they were almost unable to express themselves. How could the scholars there believe this story? Their feat was really impossible.

There are two things that I will never forget: the soldiers on the Emden calling out three cheers for the captain while leaning on their guns before they died, and the scene of the French destroyer being sunk in Penang.

Speaking of the second thing, at that time I was in the ammunition lifting room. The position was very narrow, only four feet square. The two cranes in the room had already been blown up by artillery fire. The smell of burning rubber made me suffocated. The light in the room was originally only a candle. Since the oxygen supply was cut off, it also went out in a few minutes. Opening the armor door was against military orders when the battle started, so I lay in the room half-dead. Later, I heard a voice of temporary ceasefire from the intercommunication tube. I used all my strength to open the iron door and walked onto the deck to breathe life-saving air.

I forgot everything when I came back to life. The rising sun rose from the sea, and a golden half of the sun appeared in the darkness. Looking over, there was half of the stern of the enemy ship sticking out of the water. We could also hear the sound of the engine running. Four seconds later, the ship shook and rolled over, and in an instant, it sank to the bottom of the water. At this time, I couldn't help but reflect on philosophy, silently watching the sun created by God and sending off the man-made ship sinking. This incident was even more shocking than the scene of the Matlas oil tank exploding and the fire was blazing. (End)

Social News Submission Guidelines 225

(1) The text should be about science, industry, commerce, or villages at home and abroad.

(2) Health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life and other news activities are limited to paintings of various social life sentiments. (3) Photos of seasonal scenery, animals, plants, people, and news are qualified. Photos of seasonal scenery with ladies are especially welcome.

(4) Each text should be up to 2,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(6) Do not write horizontally, and do not write carelessly. Western languages can be omitted as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.
